**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

## Your Task

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

The answer.json file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Firefox DOM Event Dispatch Chain

I traced the complete DOM event dispatch chain for a click event through the Firefox gecko-dev codebase (`sg-evals/firefox--871325b8`):

### 1. Event Creation
- **`widget/BasicEvents.h`** — `WidgetEvent` base class for all native events
- **`widget/MouseEvents.h`** — `WidgetMouseEvent` and `WidgetPointerEvent` for mouse/pointer events
- **`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`** — `EventDispatcher::CreateEvent()` lazily creates DOM Event wrappers
- **`dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp`** — `InitAndDispatchClickEvent()` creates click events from mouseup

### 2. Event Target Identification
- **`layout/base/PresShell.cpp`** — `PresShell::EventHandler::HandleEvent()` is the entry point; `HandleEventUsingCoordinates()` finds the DOM element under the pointer; `DispatchEventToDOM()` resolves the final target
- **`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`** — `EventDispatcher::Dispatch()` builds the event target chain by calling `EventTargetChainItem::GetEventTargetParent()` on each node up the DOM tree

### 3. Capture/Bubble Phase Traversal
- **`dom/events/EventDispatcher.cpp`** — `EventTargetChainItem::HandleEventTargetChain()` implements all three phases: capture (root→target), target, and bubble (target→root), iterating the chain array in both directions

### 4. Event Listener Invocation
- **`dom/events/EventListenerManager.cpp`** — `HandleEventInternal()` → `HandleEventWithListenerArray()` → `HandleEventSingleListener()` invokes each registered JS/XPCOM callback

### 5. Default Action Execution
- **`dom/events/EventStateManager.cpp`** — `PreHandleEvent()` runs before DOM dispatch; `PostHandleEvent()` runs after; for mouseup, `PostHandleMouseUp()` → `Dis
... (truncated)

activation behaviors (e.g., following links, submitting forms) after the event dispatch completes, if the event was not default-prevented.\\n\\n### Key Files Summary\\n\\n- **`widget/BasicEvents.h`**:
